< review>
Hardly Strictly Bluegrass is San Francisco's premier outdoor music festival, and the one that best captures the spirit of the city's musical legacy. Lindley Meadow is a big part of that. On regular days, it's dotted with picnics and lawn revelers, but during festivals, it's plastered with tarps and coolers. It is capable of hosting a wonderful atmosphere.</review>

I had a very good experience with Express Electrical Services. George is one of the most responsive, helpful, conscientious professionals I have worked with. He thoroughly diagnosed the issues (due to it being an older home,) outlined every part of the process, showed me the functions after the major steps, and ensured I was satisfied with the results. He took extra care to ensure the aesthetics of the house were not flawed by the required work (due to updated building codes.) He and his team were also very diligent about the PPE inside and out.

I'm very happy with Express Electrical and George and I will recommend them to everyone!< /Review>

<Review>I do have to be up front and say that my issue with Express Electrical is my own fault for agreeing to do service. But I feel like the result of service for the price I paid was a little shady.
I live out of state, but own a rental house in Anaheim. My tennant called and said they had lost power to a whole wall of outlets in kitchen. Express Electric did have a relatively fast response time, but when the tech got there and made his diagnosis he said since the breaker was not tripped "there is a short and I have no power".....well no duh!... thanks for that Sherlock. I was hoping he could find where the short was.
There is 4 regular outlets on that wall and 2 GFCI. So he said that he would find the short and replace any wire in the wall and outlets that are damaged from the short circuit and it would cost me $1000.00.
Me, not being an electrician thought a short would be something in the wall, so I thought this was a great deal.
2 hours after I approved, i called my tennant to ask what progress the tech has made thinking he was still working on it... my tennant replied that the tech was already done and gone. I had received no pictures, diagnosis, or invoice at the time of service. I asked my tennant what the issue was and how response was, " he found a loose wire behind a GFCI. He tightened it up and we had power."
So for me..... I understand I agreed to $1000 for something that could have been some work.... but when it came to light that it was just a freaking loose wire and no wire or equipment needed to be replaced, I would have assumed that Express Electric would have adjusted the price at least a little. But no, I received no notifications until the emailed invoice later that night, charging $1080.... I would have be much happier paying someone $150 per hour and putting all new outlets in....
Then I missed a call 2 days later and got a voicemail about how I liked my service. When I tried to call back, I got someone else, explained my frustration, she said she would let the customer service rep know to call me back.... but I heard nothing.. ever again.
Really Express Electric... be a better company!!!  I have many properties in CA, but you are one company I will not be calling back.

<UserId.>106054428328848843624<//UserId.><user_name>S. M. ‚ÄúI'm not the one‚Äù Newlin<//user_name>< Date>
1619669419175<//Date>
< Rate>
5< /Rate>
< Review>
I spent my childhood camping in rock creek canyon. Iris meadow and French Camp, campgrounds. When my mom was a kid in the 50's she, my uncle, grandma and grandpa camped in East Fork every summer.
My mom's ashes were scattered at the lake in 1999. Now as a dad, I bring my daughter every summer to visit her; and to tell her stories about her grandma, my uncle and my grandparents adventures at Rock Creek. This canyon is the one family tradition which has transcended generations.
My daughter when she was 6 caught her very first fish, from the exact same spot where I caught my very first fish when I was 9.
I suspect there are many families who can tell tales of this place going way back, its really that... powerful, I guess. The canyon, like a container holding our most sacred relics. The stories I share with my daughter at the campfire, every year. In that canyon, I am home. Please take good care of it when you visit. It wasnt so busy 30 years ago when I was a kid.
Please pick up your fishing line, nightcrawler containers and  beer cans. Let the wind through the trees be the loudest noise we hear.
Recognize that this place is very much alive. Know that for some of us who've seen and been through the worst of mankind, the peace found in this place is second to none. For me, it's the only place on earth where I can find what I need to face the things I've lived through. Tread lightly and enjoy.</Review>

< review>
I had been going here for over 20 years. I used to love going here until they started treating me strange... <Resp>None</Resp>< text>
I have not been to a Casa Jimenez in a while. I was out with friends and family. We craved Mexican food so we stopped here in Hemet. My friends and family were from Adelanto so I didn't want to disappoint. We enjoyed every bite! Delicious just like I remember. We also had a few beers (Corona), and they were ice cold as was the soda. We almost didn't stop. Their sign was being fixed, which we didn't know, giving us the impression they were out of business. I'm glad we stopped finding out they were still open! Beef tacos, chicken chimichanga, cheese enchiladas, chili relleno, and more were all very good. This really fixed our craving for Mexican food! Prices have come up since I last visited but still well worth it. I will still be a loyal customer for years to come. I can't say enough about the staff. Attentive, courteous, prompt, and more than one person took care of our table. I hope they stay open for many years to come!< /text>

<Rate>1</Rate><text>Total let down. I've been to this Casa Jimenez many times, along with other locations; and this is the first time I've been this disappointed in the food and service. First off, we come here for the all you can eat. Turns out they only do the all you can eat between 1p and 6p. Completely different than other chains. Then trying to read their menu was not easy. Most of the stuff is in Spanish with English translations, which is fine, but it was like one big run on sentence. And between the background color, the font color, and the glare from the lighting it was simply hard to read. My husband ordered the chili Colorado and it was strange. It had a sweet thin sauce, almost like a sweet marinara sauce; instead of the normal thick chili or enchilada sauce that it normally comes with. We've been to this restuarant a few times over the course of the last few years, and were regulars many, many years ago... and this experience was the worst. <time>1541085182035<//time>< Text>
The chips were excellent,  the red salsa, not at all.  Watery, lack of flavor.  Green salsa, really good.

Ordered the combo plate, chicken taco, chile rellano,  cheese enchilada rice and beans.

The chicken taco was so over cooked that the shredded chicken was dark brown and hard like beef jerky.  The shell was tough, and overall lacked any flavor.

The cheeses enchilada was a soggy mess.

Chile rellano was full of flavor, it's a shame the center was ice cold.

Rice was soggy, too much water during cooking process.  Beans were good, hot and full of flavor, hard to mess up beans.

Wife ordered the same meal and food was exactly the same as mine.

When 3/4s of the food is left on the plate and both people do not ask for to go containers, that should be a huge red flag.

Server didnt ask us about the food.

I've been going here off and on for over 10 years, tried to give them one more chance, I'm done.

Like a dying relationship you try and hope they get better, but in a town known for below average food, a slightly less than average restaurant can seem to be a culinary oasis, when in reality, it's just another slightly below average eatery in below average food town.<//Text>
